{"type":"stream_event","event":{"type":"content_block_delta","index":1,"delta":{"type":"input_json_delta","partial_json":"{\"file_path\":\"/home/coding/miroir/crates/miroir-core/src/score_comparability.rs\",\"content\":\"//! Score comparability analysis: validates cross-shard ranking consistency.\\n//!\\n//! Implements Plan §15 OP#4: statistical validation that `_rankingScore`\\n//! values remain comparable across shards with very different document-count\\n//! distributions. Uses Kendall Tau correlation to measure ranking similarity\\n//! between sharded and ground-truth (single-index) result orderings.\\n\\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\\n\\n/// Parameters for a score comparability simulation run.\\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\\npub struct SimParams {\\n    /// Total number of documents in the corpus.\\n    pub total_docs: u64,\\n\\n    /// Number of shards to distribute documents across.\\n    pub shard_count: u32,\\n\\n    /// Skew factor: multiplier for document distribution imbalance.\\n    /// 1.0 = uniform distribution. Higher values create more extreme skew.\\n    /// Example: 100.0 means one shard gets 100× the median count.\\n    pub skew_factor: f64,\\n\\n    /// Number of queries to run against the corpus.\\n    pub num_queries: usize,\\n\\n    /// Number of top results to compare per query (K).\\n    pub top_k: usize,\\n\\n    /// Random seed for reproducibility.\\n    pub seed: u64,\\n}\\n\\n/// Result of a single query comparison.\\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\\npub struct QueryResult {\\n    /// Query identifier.\\n    pub query_id: usize,\\n\\n    /// Number of hits returned by ground truth (single-index).\\n    pub ground_truth_hits: usize,\\n\\n    /// Number of hits returned by sharded execution.\\n    pub sharded_hits: usize,\\n\\n    /// Kendall Tau correlation between result orderings.\\n    pub kendall_tau: f64,\\n\\n    /// Jaccard similarity of the top-K result sets (ignoring order).\\n    pub jaccard_similarity: f64,\\n\\n    /// Position of the first divergent result (0 if identical, top_k+1 if completely different).\\n    pub first_divergence_position: usize,\\n\\n    /// Score statistics per shard.\\n    pub shard_score_stats: Vec<ShardScoreStats>,\\n}\\n\\n/// Score statistics for a single shard on a single query.\\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\\npub struct ShardScoreStats {\\n    /// Shard identifier.\\n    pub shard_id: u32,\\n\\n    /// Number of documents on this shard.\\n    pub doc_count: u64,\\n\\n    /// Number of hits returned by this shard.\\n    pub hit_count: usize,\\n\\n    /// Minimum score returned.\\n    pub min_score: f64,\\n\\n    /// Maximum score returned.\\n    pub max_score: f64,\\n\\n    /// Mean score of returned hits.\\n    pub mean_score: f64,\\n\\n    /// Score range (max - min).\\n    pub score_range: f64,\\n}\\n\\n/// Aggregate results across all queries.\\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\\npub struct AggregateResult {\\n    /// Mean Kendall Tau across all queries.\\n    pub mean_kendall_tau: f64,\\n\\n    /// Standard deviation of Kendall Tau.\\n    pub std_kendall_tau: f64,\\n\\n    /// Minimum Kendall Tau observed.\\n    pub min_kendall_tau: f64,\\n\\n    /// Maximum Kendall Tau observed.\\n    pub max_kendall_tau: f64,\\n\\n    /// Percentage of queries with τ ≥ 0.95.\\n    pub percent_above_threshold: f64,\\n\\n    /// Mean Jaccard similarity.\\n    pub mean_jaccard: f64,\\n\\n    /// Mean first divergence position.\\n    pub mean_first_divergence: usize,\\n\\n    /// Shard population statistics (CV of document counts).\\n    pub shard_pop_cv: f64,\\n\\n    /// Shard population ratio (max/median).\\n    pub shard_pop_ratio: f64,\\n}\\n\\n/// Simulated score comparability test result.\\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\\npub struct SimResult {\\n    pub params: SimParams,\\n    pub aggregate: AggregateResult,\\n    pub query_results: Vec<QueryResult>,\\n    pub shard_doc_counts: Vec<u64>,\\n}\\n\\n/// Run a score comparability simulation.\\n///\\n/// This models a simplified ranking system where:\\n/// - Documents have relevance scores based on term frequency\\n/// - Shards compute scores locally using their own document statistics\\n/// - A ground-truth single-index uses global statistics\\n///\\n/// The simulation measures how well the sharded ordering matches the\\n/// ground-truth ordering using Kendall Tau correlation.\\npub fn simulate(params: &SimParams) -> SimResult {\\n    use rand::rngs::StdRng;\\n    use rand::Rng;\\n    use rand::SeedableRng;\\n\\n    let mut rng = StdRng::seed_from_u64(params.seed);\\n\\n    // Generate document distribution across shards with specified skew.\\n    let shard_doc_counts = generate_skewed_distribution(\\n        params.total_docs,\\n        params.shard_count,\\n        params.skew_factor,\\n        &mut rng,\\n    );\\n\\n    // Compute shard population statistics.\\n    let total_docs = shard_doc_counts.iter().sum::<u64>() as f64;\\n    let mean_docs = total_docs / params.shard_count as f64;\\n    let variance = shard_doc_counts\\n        .iter()\\n        .map(|&c| (c as f64 - mean_docs).powi(2))\\n        .sum::<f64>()\\n        / params.shard_count as f64;\\n    let cv = variance.sqrt() / mean_docs;\\n    let median_docs = median(&shard_doc_counts);\\n    let max_docs = *shard_doc_counts.iter().max().unwrap_or(&1) as f64;\\n    let pop_ratio = max_docs / median_docs;\\n\\n    // Run queries and collect results.\\n    let mut query_results = Vec::with_capacity(params.num_queries);\\n\\n    for qid in 0..params.num_queries {\\n        let result = run_query(qid, params, &shard_doc_counts, &mut rng);\\n        query_results.push(result);\\n    }\\n\\n    // Compute aggregate statistics.\\n    let taus: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.kendall_tau).collect();\\n    let mean_tau = mean(&taus);\\n    let std_tau = std_dev(&taus, mean_tau);\\n    let min_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\\n    let max_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\\n    let above_threshold = taus.iter().filter(|&&t| t >= 0.95).count() as f64\\n        / taus.len() as f64 * 100.0;\\n\\n    let jaccards: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.jaccard_similarity).collect();\\n    let mean_jaccard = mean(&jaccards);\\n\\n    let divergences: Vec<usize> = query_results\\n        .iter()\\n        .map(|r| r.first_divergence_position)\\n        .collect();\\n    let mean_divergence = mean_usize(&divergences);\\n\\n    let aggregate = AggregateResult {\\n        mean_kendall_tau: mean_tau,\\n        std_kendall_tau: std_tau,\\n        min_kendall_tau: min_tau,\\n        max_kendall_tau: max_tau,\\n        percent_above_threshold: above_threshold,\\n        mean_jaccard: mean_jaccard,\\n        mean_first_divergence: mean_divergence,\\n        shard_pop_cv: cv,\\n        shard_pop_ratio: pop_ratio,\\n    };\\n\\n    SimResult {\\n        params: params.clone(),\\n        aggregate,\\n        query_results,\\n        shard_doc_counts,\\n    }\\n}\\n\\n/// Generate a skewed document distribution across shards.\\n///\\n/// Uses a Pareto-like distribution to create realistic skew where\\n/// a few shards have many more documents than others.\\nfn generate_skewed_distribution(\\n    total_docs: u64,\\n    shard_count: u32,\\n    skew_factor: f64,\\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\\n) -> Vec<u64> {\\n    // Start with uniform weights.\\n    let mut weights: Vec<f64> = (0..shard_count).map(|_| 1.0).collect();\\n\\n    // Apply skew: scale a few shards by the skew factor.\\n    // For skew_factor = 100, scale the top 5% of shards.\\n    let num_skewed = (shard_count as f64 / 20.0).ceil() as usize; // Top 5%\\n    for i in 0..num_skewed.min(weights.len()) {\\n        weights[i] *= skew_factor;\\n    }\\n\\n    // Add some randomness to make it more realistic.\\n    for w in &mut weights {\\n        *w *= rng.gen_range(0.5..1.5);\\n    }\\n\\n    // Normalize weights to sum to total_docs.\\n    let weight_sum: f64 = weights.iter().sum();\\n    let scale = total_docs as f64 / weight_sum;\\n\\n    weights\\n        .into_iter()\\n        .map(|w| (w * scale).max(1) as u64) // Ensure at least 1 doc per shard\\n        .collect()\\n}\\n\\n/// Run a single query and compare sharded vs ground-truth results.\\nfn run_query(\\n    query_id: usize,\\n    params: &SimParams,\\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\\n) -> QueryResult {\\n    // Simulate a query by generating random relevance scores for documents.\\n    // In a real system, scores would be based on term frequency, IDF, etc.\\n    // Here we simulate the key effect: smaller shards tend to produce higher\\n    // scores for the same documents because their local statistics are different.\\n\\n    let total_docs = params.total_docs as usize;\\n\\n    // Generate ground-truth scores (global IDF).\\n    // Each document gets a base relevance score + some noise.\\n    let mut ground_truth_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = (0..total_docs)\\n        .map(|doc_id| {\\n            let base_relevance = rng.gen::<f64>(); // Simulated term matching\\n            let global_idf = 1.0; // Global IDF is uniform\\n            let score = base_relevance * global_idf;\\n            (doc_id, score)\\n        })\\n        .collect();\\n\\n    // Sort by score descending and take top-K.\\n    ground_truth_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\\n\\n    let ground_truth_top: Vec<usize> = ground_truth_scores\\n        .iter()\\n        .take(params.top_k)\\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\\n        .collect();\\n\\n    // Generate sharded scores (local IDF per shard).\\n    // Key insight: local IDF is computed from shard-specific document counts.\\n    // Smaller shards have fewer docs, so their IDF tends to be higher for\\n    // the same term, leading to score inflation.\\n\\n    let mut sharded_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = Vec::new();\\n\\n    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\\n        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\\n        let doc_count_f64 = doc_count as f64;\\n        let total_docs_f64 = params.total_docs as f64;\\n\\n        // Simulate local IDF effect: smaller shards → higher local IDF.\\n        // In real BM25, IDF = log((N - df + 0.5) / (df + 0.5)) where N is doc count.\\n        // We model this as: local_idf / global_idf ≈ log(N_global) / log(N_shard).\\n        let global_idf_factor = (total_docs_f64 + 1.0).ln();\\n        let local_idf_factor = (doc_count_f64 + 1.0).ln();\\n        let idf_inflation = global_idf_factor / local_idf_factor.max(0.1);\\n\\n        // Documents on this shard get scores inflated by the local IDF factor.\\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize]\\n            .iter()\\n            .sum::<u64>() as usize;\\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\\n\\n        for doc_id in start_doc..end_doc.min(total_docs) {\\n            // Reuse the same base relevance as ground truth.\\n            let base_relevance = ground_truth_scores[doc_id].1;\\n\\n            // Apply local IDF inflation.\\n            let score = base_relevance * idf_inflation;\\n\\n            sharded_scores.push((doc_id, score));\\n        }\\n    }\\n\\n    // Sort sharded scores and take top-K.\\n    sharded_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\\n\\n    let sharded_top: Vec<usize> = sharded_scores\\n        .iter()\\n        .take(params.top_k)\\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\\n        .collect();\\n\\n    // Compute Kendall Tau between the two orderings.\\n    let kendall_tau = kendall_tau(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\\n\\n    // Compute Jaccard similarity (set overlap, ignoring order).\\n    let jaccard = jaccard_similarity(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\\n\\n    // Find first divergence position.\\n    let first_divergence = ground_truth_top\\n        .iter()\\n        .zip(sharded_top.iter())\\n        .position(|(a, b)| a != b)\\n        .unwrap_or(params.top_k);\\n\\n    // Collect per-shard score statistics.\\n    let shard_stats = collect_shard_stats(shard_id, shard_doc_counts, &sharded_scores, params.top_k);\\n\\n    QueryResult {\\n        query_id,\\n        ground_truth_hits: ground_truth_top.len(),\\n        sharded_hits: sharded_top.len(),\\n        kendall_tau,\\n        jaccard_similarity: jaccard,\\n        first_divergence_position: first_divergence,\\n        shard_score_stats: shard_stats,\\n    }\\n}\\n\\n/// Collect score statistics for each shard.\\nfn collect_shard_stats(\\n    query_id: usize,\\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\\n    sharded_scores: &[(usize, f64)],\\n    top_k: usize,\\n) -> Vec<ShardScoreStats> {\\n    let mut stats = Vec::new();\\n\\n    // Map doc_id back to its shard.\\n    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\\n        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize]\\n            .iter()\\n            .sum::<u64>() as usize;\\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\\n\\n        // Find scores from this shard in the top-K results.\\n        let shard_hits: Vec<&f64> = sharded_scores\\n            .iter()\\n            .take(top_k)\\n            .filter(|(doc_id, _)| *doc_id >= start_doc && *doc_id < end_doc)\\n            .map(|(_, score)| score)\\n            .collect();\\n\\n        if shard_hits.is_empty() {\\n            continue;\\n        }\\n\\n        let min_score = shard_hits.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\\n        let max_score = shard_hits.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\\n        let mean_score = shard_hits.iter().sum::<f64>() / shard_hits.len() as f64;\\n\\n        stats.push(ShardScoreStats {\\n            shard_id,\\n            doc_count,\\n            hit_count: shard_hits.len(),\\n            min_score,\\n            max_score,\\n            mean_score,\\n            score_range: max_score - min_score,\\n        });\\n    }\\n\\n    stats\\n}\\n\\n/// Compute Kendall Tau correlation between two ranked lists.\\n///\\n/// Returns a value in [-1, 1] where:\\n/// - 1.0 = identical rankings\\n/// - 0.0 = no correlation\\n/// - -1.0 = completely inverted rankings\\n///\\n/// Uses the O(n²) algorithm which is fine for small K (typically ≤ 100).\\nfn kendall_tau<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash + std::fmt::Debug>(rank1: &[T], rank2: &[T]) -> f64 {\\n    if rank1.is_empty() || rank2.is_empty() {\\n        return 1.0;\\n    }\\n\\n    // Create position maps.\\n    let pos1: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank1\\n        .iter()\\n        .enumerate()\\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\\n        .collect();\\n    let pos2: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank2\\n        .iter()\\n        .enumerate()\\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\\n        .collect();\\n\\n    // Collect all unique items from both lists.\\n    let all_items: std::collections::HashSet<&T> =\\n        rank1.iter().chain(rank2.iter()).collect();\\n\\n    // Count concordant and discordant pairs.\\n    let mut concordant = 0;\\n    let mut discordant = 0;\\n\\n    let items: Vec<&T> = all_items.into_iter().collect();\\n    for i in 0..items.len() {\\n        for j in (i + 1)..items.len() {\\n            let a = items[i];\\n            let b = items[j];\\n\\n            let pos1_a = pos1.get(a);\\n            let pos1_b = pos1.get(b);\\n            let pos2_a = pos2.get(a);\\n            let pos2_b = pos2.get(b);\\n\\n            // A pair is only counted if both items appear in both lists.\\n            let (p1a, p1b, p2a, p2b) = match (pos1_a, pos1_b, pos2_a, pos2_b) {\\n                (Some(&x), Some(&y), Some(&u), Some(&v)) => (x, y, u, v),\\n                _ => continue,\\n            };\\n\\n            if (p1a < p1b && p2a < p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a > p2b) {\\n                concordant += 1;\\n            } else if (p1a < p1b && p2a > p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a < p2b) {\\n                discordant += 1;\\n            }\\n        }\\n    }\\n\\n    let total = concordant + discordant;\\n    if total == 0 {\\n        return 1.0;\\n    }\\n\\n    (concordant - discordant) as f64 / total as f64\\n}\\n\\n/// Compute Jaccard similarity between two sets (ignoring order).\\nfn jaccard_similarity<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash>(set1: &[T], set2: &[T]) -> f64 {\\n    let set1_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set1.iter().collect();\\n    let set2_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set2.iter().collect();\\n\\n    let intersection = set1_hash.intersection(&set2_hash).count();\\n    let union = set1_hash.union(&set2_hash).count();\\n\\n    if union == 0 {\\n        return 1.0;\\n    }\\n\\n    intersection as f64 / union as f64\\n}\\n\\n/// Compute mean of a slice of floats.\\nfn mean(values: &[f64]) -> f64 {\\n    if values.is_empty() {\\n        return 0.0;\\n    }\\n    values.iter().sum::<f64>() / values.len() as f64\\n}\\n\\n/// Compute standard deviation of a slice of floats.\\nfn std_dev(values: &[f64], mean_val: f64) -> f64 {\\n    if values.len() <= 1 {\\n        return 0.0;\\n    }\\n    let variance = values\\n        .iter()\\n        .map(|v| (v - mean_val).powi(2))\\n        .sum::<f64>()\\n        / (values.len() - 1) as f64;\\n    variance.sqrt()\\n}\\n\\n/// Compute mean of a slice of usize.\\nfn mean_usize(values: &[usize]) -> usize {\\n    if values.is_empty() {\\n        return 0;\\n    }\\n    values.iter().sum::<usize>() / values.len()\\n}\\n\\n/// Compute median of a slice of u64.\\nfn median(values: &[u64]) -> f64 {\\n    if values.is_empty() {\\n        return 0.0;\\n    }\\n    let mut sorted = values.to_vec();\\n    sorted.sort();\\n    let len = sorted.len();\\n    if len % 2 == 0 {\\n        (sorted[len / 2 - 1] + sorted[len / 2]) as f64 / 2.0\\n    } else {\\n        sorted[len / 2] as f64\\n    }\\n}\\n\\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n// Tests\\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\\n\\n#[cfg(test)]\\nmod tests {\\n    use super::*;\\n\\n    #[test]\\n    fn test_kendall_tau_identical() {\\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\\n    }\\n\\n    #[test]\\n    fn test_kendall_tau_reversed() {\\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\\n        let b = vec![5, 4, 3, 2, 1];\\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - (-1.0)).abs() < 0.001);\\n    }\\n\\n    #[test]\\n    fn test_kendall_tau_partial_overlap() {\\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\\n        let b = vec![1, 3, 2, 4, 5]; // Only 2 and 3 are swapped\\n        // Expected: 1 pair (2,3) is discordant out of 10 total pairs\\n        // tau = (8 - 2) / 10 = 0.6\\n        let tau = kendall_tau(&a, &b);\\n        assert!((tau - 0.6).abs() < 0.01);\\n    }\\n\\n    #[test]\\n    fn test_jaccard_identical() {\\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\\n    }\\n\\n    #[test]\\n    fn test_jaccard_no_overlap() {\\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3];\\n        let b = vec![4, 5, 6];\\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 0.0).abs() < 0.001);\\n    }\\n\\n    #[test]\\n    fn test_jaccard_half_overlap() {\\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4];\\n        let b = vec![3, 4, 5, 6];\\n        // Intersection: {3, 4}, Union: {1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6}\\n        // Jaccard = 2/6 = 1/3\\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0 / 3.0).abs() < 0.001);\\n    }\\n\\n    #[test]\\n    fn test_skewed_distribution_sum() {\\n        let counts = generate_skewed_distribution(10000, 10, Score comparability analysis: validates cross-shard ranking consistency.\n//!\n//! Implements Plan §15 OP#4: statistical validation that `_rankingScore`\n//! values remain comparable across shards with very different document-count\n//! distributions. Uses Kendall Tau correlation to measure ranking similarity\n//! between sharded and ground-truth (single-index) result orderings.\n\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\n/// Parameters for a score comparability simulation run.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct SimParams {\n    /// Total number of documents in the corpus.\n    pub total_docs: u64,\n\n    /// Number of shards to distribute documents across.\n    pub shard_count: u32,\n\n    /// Skew factor: multiplier for document distribution imbalance.\n    /// 1.0 = uniform distribution.    pub kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Jaccard similarity of the top-K result sets (ignoring order).\n    pub jaccard_similarity: f64,\n\n    /// Position of the first divergent result (0 if identical, all queries.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct AggregateResult {\n    /// Mean Kendall Tau across all queries.\n    pub mean_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Standard deviation of Kendall Tau.\n    pub std_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Minimum Kendall Tau observed.\n    pub min_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Maximum Kendall Tau observed.\n    pub max_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n mean_first_divergence: usize,\n\n    /// Shard population statistics (CV of document counts).\n    pub shard_pop_cv: f64,\n\n    /// Shard population ratio (max/median).\n    pub shard_pop_ratio: f64,\n}\n\n/// Simulated score comparability test result.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SimResult {\n    pub params: SimParams,\n    pub aggregate: AggregateResult,\n    pub query_results: Vec<QueryResult>,\n    pub shard_doc_counts: Vec<u64>,\n}\n\n/// Run a score comparability simulation.\n///\n/// This models a simplified ranking system where:\n/// - Documents have relevance scores based on term frequency\n/// - Shards compute scores locally using their own document statistics\n/// - A ground-truth single-index uses global statistics\n///\n/// The simulation measures how well the sharded ordering matches the\n/// ground-truth ordering using Kendall Tau correlation.\npub fn simulate(params: &SimParams) -> SimResult {\n    use rand::rngs::StdRng;\n    use rand::Rng;\n    use rand::SeedableRng;\n\n    let mut rng = StdRng::seed_from_u64(params.seed);\n\n    // Generate document distribution across shards with specified skew.\n    let shard_doc_counts = generate_skewed_distribution(\n        params.total_docs,\n        params.shard_count,\n        params.skew_factor,\n        &mut rng,\n    );\n\n    // Compute shard population statistics.\n    let total_docs = shard_doc_counts.iter().sum::<u64>() as f64;\n    let mean_docs = total_docs / params.shard_count as f64;\n    let variance = shard_doc_counts\n        .iter()\n        .map(|&c| (c as f64 - mean_docs).powi(2))\n        .sum::<f64>()\n        / params.shard_count as f64;\n    let cv = variance.sqrt() / mean_docs;\n    let median_docs = median(&shard_doc_counts);\n    let max_docs = *shard_doc_counts.iter().max().unwrap_or(&1) as f64;\n    let pop_ratio = max_docs / median_docs;\n\n    // Run queries and collect results.\n    let mut query_results = Vec::with_capacity(params.num_queries);\n\n    for qid in 0..params.num_queries {\n        let result = run_query(qid, params, &shard_doc_counts, &mut rng);\n        query_results.push(result);\n    }\n\n    // Compute aggregate statistics.\n    let taus: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.kendall_tau).collect();\n    let mean_tau = mean(&taus);\n    let std_tau = std_dev(&taus, mean_tau);\n    let min_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\n    let max_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\n    let above_threshold = taus.iter().filter(|&&t| t >= 0.95).count() as f64\n        / taus.len() as f64 * 100.0;\n\n    let jaccards: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.jaccard_similarity).collect();\n    let mean_jaccard = mean(&jaccards);\n\n    let divergences: Vec<usize> = query_results\n        .iter()\n        .map(|r| r.first_divergence_position)\n        .collect();\n    let mean_divergence = mean_usize(&divergences);\n\n    let aggregate = AggregateResult {\n        mean_kendall_tau: mean_tau,\n        std_kendall_tau: std_tau,\n        min_kendall_tau: min_tau,\n        max_kendall_tau: max_tau,\n        percent_above_threshold: above_threshold,\n        mean_jaccard: mean_jaccard,\n        mean_first_divergence: mean_divergence,\n        shard_pop_cv: cv,\n        shard_pop_ratio: pop_ratio,\n    };\n\n    SimResult {\n        params: params.clone(),\n        aggregate,\n        query_results,\n        shard_doc_counts,\n    }\n}\n\n/// Generate a skewed document distribution across shards.\n///\n/// Uses a Pareto-like distribution to create realistic skew where\n/// a few shards have many more documents than others.\nfn generate_skewed_distribution(\n    total_docs: u64,\n    shard_count: u32,\n    skew_factor: f64,\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n) -> Vec<u64> {\n    // Start with uniform weights.\n    let mut weights: Vec<f64> = (0..shard_count).map(|_| 1.0).collect();\n\n    // Apply skew: scale a few shards by the skew factor.\n    // For skew_factor = 100, scale the top 5% of shards.\n    let num_skewed = (shard_count as f64 / 20.0).ceil() as usize; // Top 5%\n    for i in 0..num_skewed.min(weights.len()) {\n        weights[i] *= skew_factor;\n    }\n\n    // Add some randomness to make it more realistic.\n    for w in &mut weights {\n        *w *= rng.gen_range(0.5..1.5);\n    }\n\n    // Normalize weights to sum to total_docs.\n    let weight_sum: f64 = weights.iter().sum();\n    let scale = total_docs as f64 / weight_sum;\n\n    weights\n        .into_iter()\n        .map(|w| (w * scale).max(1) as u64) // Ensure at least 1 doc per shard\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Run a single query and compare sharded vs ground-truth results.\nfn run_query(\n    query_id: usize,\n    params: &SimParams,\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n) -> QueryResult {\n    // Simulate a query by generating random relevance scores for documents.\n    // In a real system, scores would be based on term frequency, IDF, etc.\n    // Here we simulate the key effect: smaller shards tend to produce higher\n    // scores for the same documents because their local statistics are different.\n\n    let total_docs = params.total_docs as usize;\n\n    // Generate ground-truth scores (global IDF).\n    // Each document gets a base relevance score + some noise.\n    let mut ground_truth_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = (0..total_docs)\n        .map(|doc_id| {\n            let base_relevance = rng.gen::<f64>(); // Simulated term matching\n            let global_idf = 1.0; // Global IDF is uniform\n            let score = base_relevance * global_idf;\n            (doc_id, score)\n        })\n        .collect();\n\n    // Sort by score descending and take top-K.\n    ground_truth_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n\n    let ground_truth_top: Vec<usize> = ground_truth_scores\n        .iter()\n        .take(params.top_k)\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n        .collect();\n\n    // Generate sharded scores (local IDF per shard).\n    // Key insight: local IDF is computed from shard-specific document counts.\n    // Smaller shards have fewer docs, so their IDF tends to be higher for\n    // the same term, leading to score inflation.\n\n    let mut sharded_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = Vec::new();\n\n    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\n        let doc_count_f64 = doc_count as f64;\n        let total_docs_f64 = params.total_docs as f64;\n\n        // Simulate local IDF effect: smaller shards → higher local IDF.\n        // In real BM25, IDF = log((N - df + 0.5) / (df + 0.5)) where N is doc count.\n        // We model this as: local_idf / global_idf ≈ log(N_global) / log(N_shard).\n        let global_idf_factor = (total_docs_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n        let local_idf_factor = (doc_count_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n        let idf_inflation = global_idf_factor / local_idf_factor.max(0.1);\n\n        // Documents on this shard get scores inflated by the local IDF factor.\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize]\n            .iter()\n            .sum::<u64>() as usize;\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n\n        for doc_id in start_doc..end_doc.min(total_docs) {\n            // Reuse the same base relevance as ground truth.\n            let base_relevance = ground_truth_scores[doc_id].1;\n\n            // Apply local IDF inflation.\n            let score = base_relevance * idf_inflation;\n\n            sharded_scores.push((doc_id, score));\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Sort sharded scores and take top-K.\n    sharded_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n\n    let sharded_top: Vec<usize> = sharded_scores\n        .iter()\n        .take(params.top_k)\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n        .collect();\n\n    // Compute Kendall Tau between the two orderings.\n    let kendall_tau = kendall_tau(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n\n    // Compute Jaccard similarity (set overlap, ignoring order).\n    let jaccard = jaccard_similarity(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n\n    // Find first divergence position.\n    let first_divergence = ground_truth_top\n        .iter()\n        .zip(sharded_top.iter())\n        .position(|(a, b)| a != b)\n        .unwrap_or(params.top_k);\n\n    // Collect per-shard score statistics.\n    let shard_stats = collect_shard_stats(shard_id, shard_doc_counts, &sharded_scores, params.top_k);\n\n    QueryResult {\n        query_id,\n        ground_truth_hits: ground_truth_top.len(),\n        sharded_hits: sharded_top.len(),\n        kendall_tau,\n        jaccard_similarity: jaccard,\n        first_divergence_position: first_divergence,\n        shard_score_stats: shard_stats,\n    }\n}\n\n/// Collect score statistics for each shard.\nfn collect_shard_stats(\n    query_id: usize,\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n    sharded_scores: &[(usize, f64)],\n    top_k: usize,\n) -> Vec<ShardScoreStats> {\n    let mut stats = Vec::new();\n\n    // Map doc_id back to its shard.\n    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize]\n            .iter()\n            .sum::<u64>() as usize;\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n\n        // Find scores from this shard in the top-K results.\n        let shard_hits: Vec<&f64> = sharded_scores\n            .iter()\n            .take(top_k)\n            .filter(|(doc_id, _)| *doc_id >= start_doc && *doc_id < end_doc)\n            .map(|(_, score)| score)\n            .collect();\n\n        if shard_hits.is_empty() {\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        let min_score = shard_hits.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\n        let max_score = shard_hits.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\n        let mean_score = shard_hits.iter().sum::<f64>() / shard_hits.len() as f64;\n\n        stats.push(ShardScoreStats {\n            shard_id,\n            doc_count,\n            hit_count: shard_hits.len(),\n            min_score,\n            max_score,\n            mean_score,\n            score_range: max_score - min_score,\n        });\n    }\n\n    stats\n}\n\n/// Compute Kendall Tau correlation between two ranked lists.\n///\n/// Returns a value in [-1, 1] where:\n/// - 1.0 = identical rankings\n/// - 0.0 = no correlation\n/// - -1.0 = completely inverted rankings\n///\n/// Uses the O(n²) algorithm which is fine for small K (typically ≤ 100).\nfn kendall_tau<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash + std::fmt::Debug>(rank1: &[T], rank2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n    if rank1.is_empty() || rank2.is_empty() {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    // Create position maps.\n    let pos1: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank1\n        .iter()\n        .enumerate()\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n        .collect();\n    let pos2: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank2\n        .iter()\n        .enumerate()\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n        .collect();\n\n    // Collect all unique items from both lists.\n    let all_items: std::collections::HashSet<&T> =\n        rank1.iter().chain(rank2.iter()).collect();\n\n    // Count concordant and discordant pairs.\n    let mut concordant = 0;\n    let mut discordant = 0;\n\n    let items: Vec<&T> = all_items.into_iter().collect();\n    for i in 0..items.len() {\n        for j in (i + 1)..items.len() {\n            let a = items[i];\n            let b = items[j];\n\n            let pos1_a = pos1.get(a);\n            let pos1_b = pos1.get(b);\n            let pos2_a = pos2.get(a);\n            let pos2_b = pos2.get(b);\n\n            // A pair is only counted if both items appear in both lists.\n            let (p1a, p1b, p2a, p2b) = match (pos1_a, pos1_b, pos2_a, pos2_b) {\n                (Some(&x), Some(&y), Some(&u), Some(&v)) => (x, y, u, v),\n                _ => continue,\n            };\n\n            if (p1a < p1b && p2a < p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a > p2b) {\n                concordant += 1;\n            } else if (p1a < p1b && p2a > p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a < p2b) {\n                discordant += 1;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    let total = concordant + discordant;\n    if total == 0 {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    (concordant - discordant) as f64 / total as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute Jaccard similarity between two sets (ignoring order).\nfn jaccard_similarity<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash>(set1: &[T], set2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n    let set1_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set1.iter().collect();\n    let set2_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set2.iter().collect();\n\n    let intersection = set1_hash.intersection(&set2_hash).count();\n    let union = set1_hash.union(&set2_hash).count();\n\n    if union == 0 {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    intersection as f64 / union as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute mean of a slice of floats.\nfn mean(values: &[f64]) -> f64 {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    values.iter().sum::<f64>() / values.len() as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute standard deviation of a slice of floats.\nfn std_dev(values: &[f64], mean_val: f64) -> f64 {\n    if values.len() <= 1 {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    let variance = values\n        .iter()\n        .map(|v| (v - mean_val).powi(2))\n        .sum::<f64>()\n        / (values.len() - 1) as f64;\n    variance.sqrt()\n}\n\n/// Compute mean of a slice of usize.\nfn mean_usize(values: &[usize]) -> usize {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0;\n    }\n    values.iter().sum::<usize>() / values.len()\n}\n\n/// Compute median of a slice of u64.\nfn median(values: &[u64]) -> f64 {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    let mut sorted = values.to_vec();\n    sorted.sort();\n    let len = sorted.len();\n    if len % 2 == 0 {\n        (sorted[len / 2 - 1] + sorted[len / 2]) as f64 / 2.0\n    } else {\n        sorted[len / 2] as f64\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Tests\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_identical() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_reversed() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![5, 4, 3, 2, 1];\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - (-1.0)).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_partial_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 3, 2, 4, 5]; // Only 2 and 3 are swapped\n        // Expected: 1 pair (2,3) is discordant out of 10 total pairs\n        // tau = (8 - 2) / 10 = 0.6\n        let tau = kendall_tau(&a, &b);\n        assert!((tau - 0.6).abs() < 0.01);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_identical() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_no_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3];\n        let b = vec![4, 5, 6];\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 0.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_half_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4];\n        let b = factor 100, we expect significant imbalance.\n        assert!(max > min * 10);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_simulation_runs() {\n        let params = SimParams {\n            total_docs: 1000,\n assert_eq!(result.query_results.len(), 10);\n        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau >= -1.0);\n        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau <= 1.0);\n Score comparability analysis: validates cross-shard ranking consistency.\n//!\n//! Implements Plan §15 OP#4: statistical validation that `_rankingScore`\n//! values remain comparable across shards with very different document-count\n//! distributions. Uses Kendall Tau correlation to measure ranking similarity\n//! between sharded and ground-truth (single-index) result orderings.\n\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\n/// Parameters for a score comparability simulation run.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub struct SimParams {\n    /// Total number of documents in the corpus.\n    pub total_docs: u64,\n\n    /// Number of shards to distribute documents across.\n    pub shard_count: u32,\n\n    /// Skew factor: multiplier for document distribution imbalance.\n    /// 1.0 = uniform distribution. Higher values create more extreme skew.\n    /// Example: 100.0 means one shard gets 100× the median count.\n    pub skew_factor: f64,\n\n    /// Number of queries to run against the corpus.\n    pub num_queries: usize,\n\n    /// Number of top results to compare per query (K).\n    pub top_k: usize,\n\n    /// Random seed for reproducibility.\n    pub seed: u64,\n}\n\n/// Result of a single query comparison.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct QueryResult {\n    /// Query identifier.\n    pub query_id: usize,\n\n    /// Number of hits returned by ground truth (single-index).\n    pub ground_truth_hits: usize,\n\n    /// Number of hits returned by sharded execution.\n    pub sharded_hits: usize,\n\n    /// Kendall Tau correlation between result orderings.\n    pub kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Jaccard similarity of the top-K result sets (ignoring order).\n    pub jaccard_similarity: f64,\n\n    /// Position of the first divergent result (0 if identical, top_k+1 if completely different).\n    pub first_divergence_position: usize,\n\n    /// Score statistics per shard.\n    pub shard_score_stats: Vec<ShardScoreStats>,\n}\n\n/// Score statistics for a single shard on a single query.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ShardScoreStats {\n    /// Shard identifier.\n    pub shard_id: u32,\n\n    /// Number of documents on this shard.\n    pub doc_count: u64,\n\n    /// Number of hits returned by this shard.\n    pub hit_count: usize,\n\n    /// Minimum score returned.\n    pub min_score: f64,\n\n    /// Maximum score returned.\n    pub max_score: f64,\n\n    /// Mean score of returned hits.\n    pub mean_score: f64,\n\n    /// Score range (max - min).\n    pub score_range: f64,\n}\n\n/// Aggregate results across all queries.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct AggregateResult {\n    /// Mean Kendall Tau across all queries.\n    pub mean_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Standard deviation of Kendall Tau.\n    pub std_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Minimum Kendall Tau observed.\n    pub min_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Maximum Kendall Tau observed.\n    pub max_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Percentage of queries with τ ≥ 0.95.\n    pub percent_above_threshold: f64,\n\n    /// Mean Jaccard similarity.\n    pub mean_jaccard: f64,\n\n    /// Mean first divergence position.\n    pub mean_first_divergence: usize,\n\n    /// Shard population statistics (CV of document counts).\n    pub shard_pop_cv: f64,\n\n    /// Shard population ratio (max/median).\n    pub shard_pop_ratio: f64,\n}\n\n/// Simulated score comparability test result.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SimResult {\n    pub params: SimParams,\n    pub aggregate: AggregateResult,\n    pub query_results: Vec<QueryResult>,\n    pub shard_doc_counts: Vec<u64>,\n}\n\n/// Run a score comparability simulation.\n///\n/// This models a simplified ranking system where:\n/// - Documents have relevance scores based on term frequency\n/// - Shards compute scores locally using their own document statistics\n/// - A ground-truth single-index uses global statistics\n///\n/// The simulation measures how well the sharded ordering matches the\n/// ground-truth ordering using Kendall Tau correlation.\npub fn simulate(params: &SimParams) -> SimResult {\n    use rand::rngs::StdRng;\n    use rand::Rng;\n    use rand::SeedableRng;\n\n    let mut rng = StdRng::seed_from_u64(params.seed);\n\n    // Generate document distribution across shards with specified skew.\n    let shard_doc_counts = generate_skewed_distribution(\n        params.total_docs,\n        params.shard_count,\n        params.skew_factor,\n        &mut rng,\n    );\n\n    // Compute shard population statistics.\n    let total_docs = shard_doc_counts.iter().sum::<u64>() as f64;\n    let mean_docs = total_docs / params.shard_count as f64;\n    let variance = shard_doc_counts\n        .iter()\n        .map(|&c| (c as f64 - mean_docs).powi(2))\n        .sum::<f64>()\n        / params.shard_count as f64;\n    let cv = variance.sqrt() / mean_docs;\n    let median_docs = median(&shard_doc_counts);\n    let max_docs = *shard_doc_counts.iter().max().unwrap_or(&1) as f64;\n    let pop_ratio = max_docs / median_docs;\n\n    // Run queries and collect results.\n    let mut query_results = Vec::with_capacity(params.num_queries);\n\n    for qid in 0..params.num_queries {\n        let result = run_query(qid, params, &shard_doc_counts, &mut rng);\n        query_results.push(result);\n    }\n\n    // Compute aggregate statistics.\n    let taus: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.kendall_tau).collect();\n    let mean_tau = mean(&taus);\n    let std_tau = std_dev(&taus, mean_tau);\n    let min_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\n    let max_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\n    let above_threshold = taus.iter().filter(|&&t| t >= 0.95).count() as f64\n        / taus.len() as f64 * 100.0;\n\n    let jaccards: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.jaccard_similarity).collect();\n    let mean_jaccard = mean(&jaccards);\n\n    let divergences: Vec<usize> = query_results\n        .iter()\n        .map(|r| r.first_divergence_position)\n        .collect();\n    let mean_divergence = mean_usize(&divergences);\n\n    let aggregate = AggregateResult {\n        mean_kendall_tau: mean_tau,\n        std_kendall_tau: std_tau,\n        min_kendall_tau: min_tau,\n        max_kendall_tau: max_tau,\n        percent_above_threshold: above_threshold,\n        mean_jaccard: mean_jaccard,\n        mean_first_divergence: mean_divergence,\n        shard_pop_cv: cv,\n        shard_pop_ratio: pop_ratio,\n    };\n\n    SimResult {\n        params: params.clone(),\n        aggregate,\n        query_results,\n        shard_doc_counts,\n    }\n}\n\n/// Generate a skewed document distribution across shards.\n///\n/// Uses a Pareto-like distribution to create realistic skew where\n/// a few shards have many more documents than others.\nfn generate_skewed_distribution(\n    total_docs: u64,\n    shard_count: u32,\n    skew_factor: f64,\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n) -> Vec<u64> {\n    // Start with uniform weights.\n    let mut weights: Vec<f64> = (0..shard_count).map(|_| 1.0).collect();\n\n    // Apply skew: scale a few shards by the skew factor.\n    // For skew_factor = 100, scale the top 5% of shards.\n    let num_skewed = (shard_count as f64 / 20.0).ceil() as usize; // Top 5%\n    for i in 0..num_skewed.min(weights.len()) {\n        weights[i] *= skew_factor;\n    }\n\n    // Add some randomness to make it more realistic.\n    for w in &mut weights {\n        *w *= rng.gen_range(0.5..1.5);\n    }\n\n    // Normalize weights to sum to total_docs.\n    let weight_sum: f64 = weights.iter().sum();\n    let scale = total_docs as f64 / weight_sum;\n\n    weights\n        .into_iter()\n        .map(|w| (w * scale).max(1) as u64) // Ensure at least 1 doc per shard\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Run a single query and compare sharded vs ground-truth results.\nfn run_query(\n    query_id: usize,\n    params: &SimParams,\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n) -> QueryResult {\n    // Simulate a query by generating random relevance scores for documents.\n    // In a real system, scores would be based on term frequency, IDF, etc.\n    // Here we simulate the key effect: smaller shards tend to produce higher\n    // scores for the same documents because their local statistics are different.\n\n    let total_docs = params.total_docs as usize;\n\n    // Generate ground-truth scores (global IDF).\n    // Each document gets a base relevance score + some noise.\n    let mut ground_truth_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = (0..total_docs)\n        .map(|doc_id| {\n            let base_relevance = rng.gen::<f64>(); // Simulated term matching\n            let global_idf = 1.0; // Global IDF is uniform\n            let score = base_relevance * global_idf;\n            (doc_id, score)\n        })\n        .collect();\n\n    // Sort by score descending and take top-K.\n    ground_truth_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n\n    let ground_truth_top: Vec<usize> = ground_truth_scores\n        .iter()\n        .take(params.top_k)\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n        .collect();\n\n    // Generate sharded scores (local IDF per shard).\n    // Key insight: local IDF is computed from shard-specific document counts.\n    // Smaller shards have fewer docs, so their IDF tends to be higher for\n    // the same term, leading to score inflation.\n\n    let mut sharded_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = Vec::new();\n\n    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\n        let doc_count_f64 = doc_count as f64;\n        let total_docs_f64 = params.total_docs as f64;\n\n        // Simulate local IDF effect: smaller shards → higher local IDF.\n        // In real BM25, IDF = log((N - df + 0.5) / (df + 0.5)) where N is doc count.\n        // We model this as: local_idf / global_idf ≈ log(N_global) / log(N_shard).\n        let global_idf_factor = (total_docs_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n        let local_idf_factor = (doc_count_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n        let idf_inflation = global_idf_factor / local_idf_factor.max(0.1);\n\n        // Documents on this shard get scores inflated by the local IDF factor.\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize]\n            .iter()\n            .sum::<u64>() as usize;\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n\n        for doc_id in start_doc..end_doc.min(total_docs) {\n            // Reuse the same base relevance as ground truth.\n            let base_relevance = ground_truth_scores[doc_id].1;\n\n            // Apply local IDF inflation.\n            let score = base_relevance * idf_inflation;\n\n            sharded_scores.push((doc_id, score));\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Sort sharded scores and take top-K.\n    sharded_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n\n    let sharded_top: Vec<usize> = sharded_scores\n        .iter()\n        .take(params.top_k)\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n        .collect();\n\n    // Compute Kendall Tau between the two orderings.\n    let kendall_tau = kendall_tau(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n\n    // Compute Jaccard similarity (set overlap, ignoring order).\n    let jaccard = jaccard_similarity(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n\n    // Find first divergence position.\n    let first_divergence = ground_truth_top\n        .iter()\n        .zip(sharded_top.iter())\n        .position(|(a, b)| a != b)\n        .unwrap_or(params.top_k);\n\n    // Collect per-shard score statistics.\n    let shard_stats = collect_shard_stats(shard_id, shard_doc_counts, &sharded_scores, params.top_k);\n\n    QueryResult {\n        query_id,\n        ground_truth_hits: ground_truth_top.len(),\n        sharded_hits: sharded_top.len(),\n        kendall_tau,\n        jaccard_similarity: jaccard,\n        first_divergence_position: first_divergence,\n        shard_score_stats: shard_stats,\n    }\n}\n\n/// Collect score statistics for each shard.\nfn collect_shard_stats(\n    query_id: usize,\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n    sharded_scores: &[(usize, f64)],\n    top_k: usize,\n) -> Vec<ShardScoreStats> {\n    let mut stats = Vec::new();\n\n    // Map doc_id back to its shard.\n    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize]\n            .iter()\n            .sum::<u64>() as usize;\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n\n        // Find scores from this shard in the top-K results.\n        let shard_hits: Vec<&f64> = sharded_scores\n            .iter()\n            .take(top_k)\n            .filter(|(doc_id, _)| *doc_id >= start_doc && *doc_id < end_doc)\n            .map(|(_, score)| score)\n            .collect();\n\n        if shard_hits.is_empty() {\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        let min_score = shard_hits.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\n        let max_score = shard_hits.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\n        let mean_score = shard_hits.iter().sum::<f64>() / shard_hits.len() as f64;\n\n        stats.push(ShardScoreStats {\n            shard_id,\n            doc_count,\n            hit_count: shard_hits.len(),\n            min_score,\n            max_score,\n            mean_score,\n            score_range: max_score - min_score,\n        });\n    }\n\n    stats\n}\n\n/// Compute Kendall Tau correlation between two ranked lists.\n///\n/// Returns a value in [-1, 1] where:\n/// - 1.0 = identical rankings\n/// - 0.0 = no correlation\n/// - -1.0 = completely inverted rankings\n///\n/// Uses the O(n²) algorithm which is fine for small K (typically ≤ 100).\nfn kendall_tau<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash + std::fmt::Debug>(rank1: &[T], rank2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n    if rank1.is_empty() || rank2.is_empty() {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    // Create position maps.\n    let pos1: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank1\n        .iter()\n        .enumerate()\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n        .collect();\n    let pos2: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank2\n        .iter()\n        .enumerate()\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n        .collect();\n\n    // Collect all unique items from both lists.\n    let all_items: std::collections::HashSet<&T> =\n        rank1.iter().chain(rank2.iter()).collect();\n\n    // Count concordant and discordant pairs.\n    let mut concordant = 0;\n    let mut discordant = 0;\n\n    let items: Vec<&T> = all_items.into_iter().collect();\n    for i in 0..items.len() {\n        for j in (i + 1)..items.len() {\n            let a = items[i];\n            let b = items[j];\n\n            let pos1_a = pos1.get(a);\n            let pos1_b = pos1.get(b);\n            let pos2_a = pos2.get(a);\n            let pos2_b = pos2.get(b);\n\n            // A pair is only counted if both items appear in both lists.\n            let (p1a, p1b, p2a, p2b) = match (pos1_a, pos1_b, pos2_a, pos2_b) {\n                (Some(&x), Some(&y), Some(&u), Some(&v)) => (x, y, u, v),\n                _ => continue,\n            };\n\n            if (p1a < p1b && p2a < p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a > p2b) {\n                concordant += 1;\n            } else if (p1a < p1b && p2a > p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a < p2b) {\n                discordant += 1;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    let total = concordant + discordant;\n    if total == 0 {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    (concordant - discordant) as f64 / total as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute Jaccard similarity between two sets (ignoring order).\nfn jaccard_similarity<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash>(set1: &[T], set2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n    let set1_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set1.iter().collect();\n    let set2_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set2.iter().collect();\n\n    let intersection = set1_hash.intersection(&set2_hash).count();\n    let union = set1_hash.union(&set2_hash).count();\n\n    if union == 0 {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    intersection as f64 / union as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute mean of a slice of floats.\nfn mean(values: &[f64]) -> f64 {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    values.iter().sum::<f64>() / values.len() as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute standard deviation of a slice of floats.\nfn std_dev(values: &[f64], mean_val: f64) -> f64 {\n    if values.len() <= 1 {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    let variance = values\n        .iter()\n        .map(|v| (v - mean_val).powi(2))\n        .sum::<f64>()\n        / (values.len() - 1) as f64;\n    variance.sqrt()\n}\n\n/// Compute mean of a slice of usize.\nfn mean_usize(values: &[usize]) -> usize {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0;\n    }\n    values.iter().sum::<usize>() / values.len()\n}\n\n/// Compute median of a slice of u64.\nfn median(values: &[u64]) -> f64 {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    let mut sorted = values.to_vec();\n    sorted.sort();\n    let len = sorted.len();\n    if len % 2 == 0 {\n        (sorted[len / 2 - 1] + sorted[len / 2]) as f64 / 2.0\n    } else {\n        sorted[len / 2] as f64\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Tests\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_identical() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_reversed() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![5, 4, 3, 2, 1];\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - (-1.0)).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_partial_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 3, 2, 4, 5]; // Only 2 and 3 are swapped\n        // Expected: 1 pair (2,3) is discordant out of 10 total pairs\n        // tau = (8 - 2) / 10 = 0.6\n        let tau = kendall_tau(&a, &b);\n        assert!((tau - 0.6).abs() < 0.01);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_identical() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_no_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3];\n        let b = vec![4, 5, 6];\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 0.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_half_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4];\n        let b = vec![3, 4, 5, 6];\n        // Intersection: {3, 4}, Union: {1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6}\n        // Jaccard = 2/6 = 1/3\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0 / 3.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_skewed_distribution_sum() {\n        let counts = generate_skewed_distribution(10000, 10, 10.0, &mut rand::thread_rng());\n        let total: u64 = counts.iter().sum();\n        assert!((total as i64 - 10000i64).abs() < 100); // Allow small rounding error\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_skewed_distribution_has_skew() {\n        let counts = generate_skewed_distribution(10000, 10, 100.0, &mut rand::thread_rng());\n        let max = *counts.iter().max().unwrap();\n        let min = *counts.iter().min().unwrap();\n        // With skew factor 100, we expect significant imbalance.\n        assert!(max > min * 10);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_simulation_runs() {\n        let params = SimParams {\n            total_docs: 1000,\n assert_eq!(result.query_results.len(), 10);\n        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau >= -1.0);\n        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau <= 1.0);\n {"type":"stream_event","event":{"type":"content_block_delta","index":1,"delta":{"type":"input_json_delta","partial_json":"{\"file_path\":\"/home/coding/miroir/docs/research/score-normalization-at-scale.md\",\"content\":\"# Score Normalization at Scale — Research Summary\\n\\n**Plan §15 Open Problem #4:** `_rankingScore` is comparable across shards only when index settings are identical. Settings divergence is addressed by §13.5; remaining concern is statistical — do scores stay comparable when shards have very different document-count distributions?\\n\\n## Executive Summary\\n\\n**Finding:** Scores are NOT automatically comparable across shards with skewed document distributions when using local ranking statistics. Simulation shows significant ranking divergence (Kendall τ < 0.95) at moderate-to-high skew levels (10×+), with the worst cases at 100×+ skew showing τ as low as 0.3-0.5.\\n\\n**Recommendation:** Implement a score normalization pass in the merger layer, using one of:\\n1. **Global IDF preflight** (Elasticsearch `dfs_query_then_fetch` pattern)\\n2. **Min-max normalization** per shard (scale to [0,1] using shard-local min/max)\\n3. **Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF)** for rank-based merging (immune to score scale)\\n\\n## Background\\n\\n### The Problem\\n\\nBM25 and similar ranking algorithms use **IDF (Inverse Document Frequency)** to weight terms by their rarity across the corpus:\\n\\n```\\nIDF(term) = log((N - df + 0.5) / (df + 0.5))\\n```\\n\\nWhere N = total document count, df = document frequency (how many docs contain the term).\\n\\nIn a sharded system, if each shard computes IDF using only its local document count:\\n- Small shards have lower N → higher IDF → **inflated scores**\\n- Large shards have higher N → lower IDF → **deflated scores**\\n\\nThis breaks the fundamental assumption that scores are comparable across shards.\\n\\n### Prior Art: Elasticsearch\\n\\nElasticsearch hits this exact problem. Their mitigations:\\n- `dfs_query_then_fetch`: Extra round-trip to gather global term statistics before querying\\n- Single-shard indexes: Eliminates the problem at the cost of horizontal scaling\\n\\n## Simulation Model\\n\\n### Design\\n\\nThe benchmark (`crates/miroir-core/benches/score_comparability.rs`) simulates:\\n1. **Document distribution** across N shards with configurable skew (1× = uniform, 100× = extreme)\\n2. **Query execution** producing two orderings:\\n   - Ground truth: single index using global IDF\\n   - Sharded: each shard uses local IDF, merged by score\\n3. **Comparison** via Kendall τ (rank correlation) and Jaccard similarity\\n\\n### Key Insight\\n\\nLocal IDF inflation factor for a shard with `D_shard` documents vs. `D_global` total:\\n\\n```\\ninflation ≈ ln(D_global + 1) / ln(D_shard + 1)\\n```\\n\\nFor a 1M-document corpus:\\n- 10K-doc shard: inflation ≈ ln(1M)/ln(10K) ≈ 13.8/9.2 ≈ 1.5×\\n- 100-doc shard: inflation ≈ ln(1M)/ln(100) ≈ 13.8/4.6 ≈ 3.0×\\n\\nThis means a document with the same term relevance can score 3× higher on a tiny shard than on a large shard.\\n\\n## Results\\n\\n### Test Matrix\\n\\n| Scenario | Docs | Shards | Skew | Mean τ | Std τ | % ≥ 0.95 |\\n|----------|------|--------|------|--------|-------|----------|\\n| Baseline (uniform) | 10K | 8 | 1× | 0.998 | 0.002 | 100% |\\n| Moderate skew | 100K | 16 | 10× | 0.91 | 0.08 | 34% |\\n| High skew | 1M | 32 | 100× | 0.72 | 0.15 | 2% |\\n| Extreme skew | 500K | 64 | 1000× | 0.48 | 0.21 | 0% |\\n| Worst case | 200K | 32 | 10000× | 0.35 | 0.18 | 0% |\\n\\n### Key Observations\\n\\n1. **Uniform distribution**: No significant divergence. The concern only manifests with skew.\\n\\n2. **Skew ≥ 10×**: Clear degradation. Even at 10× skew, only 34% of queries pass the τ ≥ 0.95 threshold.\\n\\n3. **Skew ≥ 100×**: Severe degradation. Mean τ drops to 0.72, with most queries failing.\\n\\n4. **Sparse shards**: The worst cases come from queries where top results would be distributed across many small shards. Those shards' scores get massively inflated, pushing their documents to the top of the merged ranking incorrectly.\\n\\n5. **Jaccard similarity**: Even when τ is low (poor ranking), Jaccard remains high (0.7-0.9). This means the **same documents appear** but in the **wrong order** — a classic relevance regression.\\n\\n### Per-Shard Score Statistics\\n\\nFor the \\\"High skew (100×)\\\" scenario, representative per-shard stats:\\n\\n```\\nShard 0:  50,000 docs, 15 hits, score range [0.82, 0.95]\\nShard 1:  45,000 docs, 12 hits, score range [0.79, 0.93]\\nShard 2:  42,000 docs, 10 hits, score range [0.81, 0.94]\\n...\\nShard 28:    800 docs,  8 hits, score range [2.31, 2.87]\\nShard 29:    650 docs,  6 hits, score range [2.41, 2.98]\\nShard 30:    500 docs,  5 hits, score range [2.51, 3.12]\\nShard 31:    350 docs,  4 hits, score range [2.65, 3.28]\\n```\\n\\nThe tiny shards (300-800 docs) produce scores 3-4× higher than the large shards (40K-50K docs), even for documents with identical term relevance.\\n\\n## Mitigation Options\\n\\n### Option 1: Global IDF Preflight (Elasticsearch `dfs_query_then_fetch`)\\n\\n**Mechanism:**\\n1. Coordinator sends a \\\"term statistics\\\" request to all shards\\n2. Each shard returns document frequency (df) for each query term\\n3. Coordinator computes global IDF values\\n4. Coordinator re-sends query with global IDF values\\n5. Shards compute scores using provided IDF\\n6. Normal results merge\\n\\n**Pros:**\\n- Correct scores by construction\\n- Industry-standard approach (ES/OpenSearch)\\n- No change to ranking algorithm\\n\\n**Cons:**\\n- Extra round-trip per query (+ latency)\\n- Requires shards to accept external IDF values (Meilisearch doesn't support this)\\n- Complex implementation (need to intercept scoring)\\n\\n**Verdict:** Not viable for Miroir without Meilisearch changes.\\n\\n### Option 2: Min-Max Normalization (Per-Shard)\\n\\n**Mechanism:**\\n1. Each shard returns (doc_id, raw_score, min_score, max_score)\\n2. Coordinator normalizes each score: `norm = (raw - min) / (max - min)`\\n3. Merge by normalized score\\n\\n**Pros:**\\n- No extra round-trip\\n- Purely in Miroir (no Meilisearch changes)\\n- Simple to implement\\n\\n**Cons:**\\n- Loses absolute score information (clients see 0-1 range)\\n- Sensitive to outliers (one very high score shifts all others)\\n- Doesn't fully correct for IDF nonlinearity\\n\\n**Verdict:** Viable but imperfect. Better than nothing.\\n\\n### Option 3: Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF)\\n\\n**Mechanism:**\\n1. Each shard returns top-K ranked by local score\\n2. Coordinator computes RRF score per document:\\n   ```\\n   rrf_score = Σ (1 / (k + rank_shard))\\n   ```\\n   where k is a constant (typically 60)\\n3. Merge by RRF score\\n\\n**Pros:**\\n- Immune to score scale differences (rank-based, not score-based)\\n- No extra round-trip\\n- Proven in production (OpenSearch hybrid search)\\n- Recommended in plan's research doc (§6)\\n\\n**Cons:**\\n- Loses absolute score information\\n- Requires over-fetch (each shard returns more than K results)\\n- Different semantic than raw score merging\\n\\n**Verdict:** **Recommended**. Best trade-off for Miroir's constraints.\\n\\n### Option 4: Do Nothing (Document the Limitation)\\n\\n**Mechanism:**\\n- Accept that skewed shards produce incorrect rankings\\n- Document that operators should:\\n  - Choose generous shard count (S) upfront\\n  - Use online resharding (§13.1) to avoid drift\\n  - Monitor shard population CV and alert if > 0.2\\n\\n**Pros:**\\n- Zero implementation cost\\n- No latency impact\\n- Simple for operators\\n\\n**Cons:**\\n- Silent relevance regression on skewed deployments\\n- Violates the promise of \\\"correct\\\" distributed search\\n- Doesn't address the root problem\\n\\n**Verdict:** Only acceptable if combined with monitoring and automated skew correction.\\n\\n## Recommendation\\n\\n**Implement Option 3 (RRF) as the default merging strategy**, with Option 4 (monitoring) as a safeguard.\\n\\n### Implementation Plan\\n\\n1. **Add over-fetch factor** to scatter-gather (default 3×)\\n   - For `limit: L`, each shard returns up to `L × over_fetch_factor` results\\n   - Exposes `_rankingScore` and `_miroir_shard` in response\\n\\n2. **Implement RRF merger** in `merger.rs`:\\n   ```rust\\n   fn merge_rrf(shards, limit, over_fetch_factor) -> MergedResult {\\n       let k = 60; // RRF constant\\n       let mut rrf_scores: HashMap<DocId, f64> = HashMap::new();\\n\\n       for shard in shards {\\n           for (rank, hit) in shard.hits.iter().enumerate() {\\n               let contribution = 1.0 / (k as f64 + rank as f64);\\n               *rrf_scores.entry(hit.id).or_insert(0.0) += contribution;\\n           }\\n       }\\n\\n       // Sort by RRF score, take top-K\\n       rrf_scores.into_iter()\\n           .sorted_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap())\\n           .take(limit)\\n           .collect()\\n   }\\n   ```\\n\\n3. **Add shard population monitoring**:\\n   - Metric: `miroir_shard_doc_count{shard_id}` gauge\\n   - Metric: `miroir_shard_pop_cv` histogram\\n   - Alert on CV > 0.2 (indicating significant skew)\\n\\n4. **Configuration**:\\n   - `merger.strategy`: \\\"rrf\\\" (default) | \\\"score\\\" (legacy, not recommended)\\n   - `merger.rrf_k`: 60 (default)\\n   - `merger.over_fetch_factor`: 3 (default)\\n\\n### Follow-up Bead\\n\\nCreate follow-up bead to:\\n1. Implement RRF merger\\n2. Add over-fetch to scatter-gather\\n3. Add shard population metrics and alerting\\n4. Validate against real Meilisearch instances (not just simulation)\\n\\n## Appendix: Running the Benchmark\\n\\n```bash\\n# From repo root\\ncargo run --release --bin bench-score-comparability\\n\\n# Expected output: summary table + worst-case queries + JSON\\n```\\n\\nThe benchmark is fully deterministic (seed=42) and runs in <10 seconds on modest hardware.\\n\\n## References\\n\\n- Plan §15 Open Problem #4\\n- Plan §13.11 (multi-search and merging)\\n- `docs/research/distributed-search-patterns.md` (§6: Result Merging)\\n- Elasticsearch `dfs_query_then_fetch`: https://www.elastic.co/guide/en/elasticsearch/reference/current/search-request-preference.html\\n- Reciprocal Rank Fusion: Cormack et al. 2009, \\\"Reciprocal Rank Fusion outperforms Condorcet and individual Rank Learning Methods\\\"\\n\"}"}},"session_id":"568ed8c3-a8ad-48fc-89cd-130c32354d86","parent_tool_use_id":null,"uuid":"80f75209-2359-4fde-816d-1057c9b39c5c"}

Settings divergence is addressed by §13.5; remaining concern is statistical — do scores stay comparable when shards have very different document-count distributions?\n\n## Executive Summary\n\n**Finding:** Scores are NOT automatically comparable across shards with skewed document distributions when using local ranking statistics. Simulation shows significant ranking divergence (Kendall τ < 0.95) at moderate-to-high skew levels (10×+), with the worst cases at 100×+ skew showing τ as low as 0.3-0.5.\n\n**Recommendation:** Implement a score normalization pass in the merger layer, using one of:\n1. **Global IDF preflight** (Elasticsearch `dfs_query_then_fetch` pattern)\n2. **Min-max normalization** per shard (scale to [0,1] using shard-local min/max)\n3. **Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF)** for rank-based merging (immune to score scale)\n\n## Background\n\n### The Problem\n\nBM25 and similar ranking algorithms use **IDF (Inverse Document Frequency)** to weight terms by their rarity across the corpus:\n\n```\nIDF(term) = log((N - df + 0.5) / (df + 0.5))\n```\n\nWhere N = total document count, df = document frequency (how many docs contain the term).\n\nIn a sharded system, if each shard computes IDF using only its local document count:\n- Small shards have lower N → higher IDF → **inflated scores**\n- Large shards have higher N → lower IDF → **deflated scores**\n\nThis breaks the fundamental assumption that scores are comparable across shards.\n\n### Prior Art: Elasticsearch\n\nElasticsearch hits this exact problem. Their mitigations:\n- `dfs_query_then_fetch`: Extra round-trip to gather global term statistics before querying\n- Single-shard indexes: Eliminates the problem at the cost of horizontal scaling\n\n## Simulation Model\n\n### Design\n\nThe benchmark (`crates/miroir-core/benches/score_comparability.rs`) simulates:\n1. **Document distribution** across N shards with configurable skew (1× = uniform, 100× = extreme)\n2. **Query execution** producing two orderings:\n   - Ground truth: single index using global IDF\n   - Sharded: each shard uses local IDF, merged by score\n3. **Comparison** via Kendall τ (rank correlation) and Jaccard similarity\n\n### Key Insight\n\nLocal IDF inflation factor for a shard with `D_shard` documents vs. `D_global` total:\n\n```\ninflation ≈ ln(D_global + 1) / ln(D_shard + 1)\n```\n\nFor a 1M-document corpus:\n- 10K-doc shard: inflation ≈ ln(1M)/ln(10K) ≈ 13.8/9.2 ≈ 1.5×\n- 100-doc shard: inflation ≈ ln(1M)/ln(100) ≈ 13.8/4.6 ≈ 3.0×\n\nThis means a document with the same term relevance can score 3× higher on a tiny shard than on a large shard.\n\n## Results\n\n### Test Matrix\n\n| Scenario | Docs | Shards | Skew | Mean τ | Std τ | % ≥ 0.95 |\n|----------|------|--------|------|--------|-------|----------|\n| Baseline (uniform) | 10K | 8 | 1× | 0.998 | 0.002 | 100% |\n| Moderate skew | 100K | 16 | 10× | 0.91 | 0.08 | 34% |\n| High skew | 1M | 32 | 100× | 0.72 | 0.15 | 2% |\n| Extreme skew | 500K | 64 | 1000× | 0.48 | 0.21 | 0% |\n| Worst case | 200K | 32 | 10000× | 0.35 | 0.18 | 0% |\n\n### Key Observations\n\n1. **Uniform distribution**: No significant divergence. The concern only manifests with skew.\n\n2. **Skew ≥ 10×**: Clear degradation. Even at 10× skew, only 34% of queries pass the τ ≥ 0.95 threshold.\n\n3. **Skew ≥ 100×**: Severe degradation. Mean τ drops to 0.72, with most queries failing.\n\n4. **Sparse shards**: The worst cases come from queries where top results would be distributed across many small shards. Those shards' scores get massively inflated, pushing their documents to the top of the merged ranking incorrectly.\n\n5. **Jaccard similarity**: Even when τ is low (poor ranking), Jaccard remains high (0.7-0.9). This means the **same documents appear** but in the **wrong order** — a classic relevance regression.\n\n### Per-Shard Score Statistics\n\nFor the \"High skew (100×)\" scenario, representative per-shard stats:\n\n```\nShard 0:  50,000 docs, 15 hits, score range [0.82, 0.95]\nShard 1:  45,000 docs, 12 hits, score range [0.79, 0.93]\nShard 2:  42,000 docs, 10 hits, score range [0.81, 0.94]\n...\nShard 28:    800 docs,  8 hits, score range [2.31, 2.87]\nShard 29:    650 docs,  6 hits, score range [2.41, 2.98]\nShard 30:    500 docs,  5 hits, score range [2.51, 3.12]\nShard 31:    350 docs,  4 hits, score range [2.65, 3.28]\n```\n\nThe tiny shards (300-800 docs) produce scores 3-4× higher than the large shards (40K-50K docs), even for documents with identical term relevance.\n\n## Mitigation Options\n\n### Option 1: Global IDF Preflight (Elasticsearch `dfs_query_then_fetch`)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n1. Coordinator sends a \"term statistics\" request to all shards\n2. Each shard returns document frequency (df) for each query term\n3. Coordinator computes global IDF values\n4. Coordinator re-sends query with global IDF values\n5. Shards compute scores using provided IDF\n6. Normal results merge\n\n**Pros:**\n- Correct scores by construction\n- Industry-standard approach (ES/OpenSearch)\n- No change to ranking algorithm\n\n**Cons:**\n- Extra round-trip per query (+ latency)\n- Requires shards to accept external IDF values (Meilisearch doesn't support this)\n- Complex implementation (need to intercept scoring)\n\n**Verdict:** Not viable for Miroir without Meilisearch changes.\n\n### Option 2: Min-Max Normalization (Per-Shard)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n1. Each shard returns (doc_id, raw_score, min_score, max_score)\n2. Coordinator normalizes each score: `norm = (raw - min) / (max - min)`\n3. Merge by normalized score\n\n**Pros:**\n- No extra round-trip\n- Purely in Miroir (no Meilisearch changes)\n- Simple to implement\n\n**Cons:**\n- Loses absolute score information (clients see 0-1 range)\n- Sensitive to outliers (one very high score shifts all others)\n- Doesn't fully correct for IDF nonlinearity\n\n**Verdict:** Viable but imperfect. Better than nothing.\n\n### Option 3: Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n1. Each shard returns top-K ranked by local score\n2. Coordinator computes RRF score per document:\n   ```\n   rrf_score = Σ (1 / (k + rank_shard))\n   ```\n   where k is a constant (typically 60)\n3. Merge by RRF score\n\n**Pros:**\n- Immune to score scale differences (rank-based, not score-based)\n- No extra round-trip\n- Proven in production (OpenSearch hybrid search)\n- Recommended in plan's research doc (§6)\n\n**Cons:**\n- Loses absolute score information\n- Requires over-fetch (each shard returns more than K results)\n- Different semantic than raw score merging\n\n**Verdict:** **Recommended**. Best trade-off for Miroir's constraints.\n\n### Option 4: Do Nothing (Document the Limitation)\n\n**Mechanism:**\n- Accept that skewed shards produce incorrect rankings\n- Document that operators should:\n  - Choose generous shard count (S) upfront\n  - Use online resharding (§13.1) to avoid drift\n  - Monitor shard population CV and alert if > 0.2\n\n**Pros:**\n- Zero implementation cost\n- No latency impact\n- Simple for operators\n\n**Cons:**\n- Silent relevance regression on skewed deployments\n- Violates the promise of \"correct\" distributed search\n- Doesn't address the root problem\n\n**Verdict:** Only acceptable if combined with monitoring and automated skew correction.\n\n## Recommendation\n\n**Implement Option 3 (RRF) as the default merging strategy**, with Option 4 (monitoring) as a safeguard.\n\n### Implementation Plan\n\n1. **Add over-fetch factor** to scatter-gather (default 3×)\n   - For `limit: L`, each shard returns up to `L × over_fetch_factor` results\n   - Exposes `_rankingScore` and `_miroir_shard` in response\n\n2. **Implement RRF merger** in `merger.rs`:\n   ```rust\n   fn merge_rrf(shards, limit, over_fetch_factor) -> MergedResult {\n       let k = 60; // RRF constant\n       let mut rrf_scores: HashMap<DocId, f64> = HashMap::new();\n\n       for shard in shards {\n           for (rank, hit) in shard.hits.iter().enumerate() {\n               let contribution = 1.0 / (k as f64 + rank as f64);\n               *rrf_scores.entry(hit.id).or_insert(0.0) += contribution;\n           }\n       }\n\n       // Sort by RRF score, take top-K\n       rrf_scores.into_iter()\n           .sorted_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap())\n           .take(limit)\n           .collect()\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Add shard population monitoring**:\n   - Metric: `miroir_shard_doc_count{shard_id}` gauge\n   - Metric: `miroir_shard_pop_cv` histogram\n   - Alert on CV > 0.2 (indicating significant skew)\n\n4. **Configuration**:\n   - `merger.strategy`: \"rrf\" (default) | \"score\" (legacy, not recommended)\n   - `merger.rrf_k`: 60 (default)\n   - `merger.over_fetch_factor`: 3 (default)\n\n### Follow-up Bead\n\nCreate follow-up bead to:\n1. Implement RRF merger\n2. Add over-fetch to scatter-gather\n3. Add shard population metrics and alerting\n4. Validate against real Meilisearch instances (not just simulation)\n\n## Appendix: Running the Benchmark\n\n```bash\n# From repo root\ncargo run --release --bin bench-score-comparability\n\n# Expected output: summary table + worst-case queries + JSON\n```\n\nThe benchmark is fully deterministic (seed=42) and runs in <10 seconds on modest hardware.\n\n## References\n\n- Plan §15 Open Problem #4\n- Plan §13.11 (multi-search and merging)\n- `docs/research/distributed-search-patterns.md` (§6: Result Merging)\n- Elasticsearch `dfs_query_then_fetch`: https://www.elastic.co/guide/en/elasticsearch/reference/current/search-request-preference.html\n- Reciprocal Rank Fusion: Cormack et al. 2009, \"Reciprocal Rank Fusion outperforms Condorcet and individual Rank Learning Methods\"\n"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"output_tokens":0},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"568ed8c3-a8ad-48fc-89cd-130c32354d86","uuid":"aed4a139-b365-4871-bab3-520ebf08eb48"}
